URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS154299281	2017-05-15 17:30:19	16210	slash	Pacific-slope/Cordilleran Flycatcher (Western Flycatcher)	Empidonax difficilis/occidentalis			1				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Clark	US-NV-003		33	USFWS_591		Desert NWR--Corn Creek (Field Station)	L168656	H	36.4387970	-115.3595660	2012-05-05	05:30:00	obsr235247	S10838974	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	420	3.219		2	1		0	1	0		Experienced an absolutely amazing migrant fallout on 5/5 at Corn Creek just north of Las Vegas.  David Donsker and I arrived at Corn Creek at first light and immediately noticed a number of kingbirds flying into the trees from the desert.  As the steady stream of birds continued, we noticed numerous warblers flying in along with the kingbirds.  The first tree we reached was loaded with Western Kingbirds, although only 10 feet tall it had at least 50 kingbirds on it perched like Christmas tree ornaments.  Each binocular field in each mulberry tree contained at least 5 Bullock's Orioles and a few more Western Kingbirds.  Groups of 5 to 10 warblers (mostly Audubon's) were in the trees, on the ground, in the grass, on fence posts - just everywhere.  We birded the oasis from 5:15 to 11 and conservatively estimated 2,000 birds of 75 species.  Counting was next to impossible as the birds were constantly flitting from tree to tree.  We returned and birded the area again from 2:30 to 5:30, and although activity was much lower, there were still hundreds of migrants, several more still flying in from the desert, and we found several species we didn't have in the morning.   Also saw 1 hybrid Eur Collared-Dove X Mourning Dove but could not determine how to enter this into e-bird.

URN:CornellLabOfOrnithology:EBIRD:OBS154847486	2019-11-05 17:03:34	16210	slash	Pacific-slope/Cordilleran Flycatcher (Western Flycatcher)	Empidonax difficilis/occidentalis			1				United States	US	Nevada	US-NV	Storey	US-NV-029		9			NV: McCarran Ranch: public entrance trailhead	L1558894	P	39.5512907	-119.5573744	2012-05-27	10:30:00	obsr18218	S10857031	Traveling	P22	EBIRD	150	6.437		2	1		0	1	0			Definitely a flycatcher. Very yellowish colors compared to most Empids stood out as prominent field mark. Very distinct wing bars and prominent eye ring. Seen from across the Truckee River, so I couldn't see the bill. I think the yellowish color makes it most probably a "Western" Flycatcher, i.e. either Pacific Slope or Cordilleran.  Based on range, Pacific Slope is perhaps less likely - there are practically no observations of it east of the mountains. There are only a few observations of Cordilleran in Nevada, but these include observations along the Truckee River in Reno and north of Fernley, by birders more competent than myself. But in migration season, I suspect either of the two could have been there, so the location by itself is not a discriminant.
